Rule Generator Message:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. This is likely due to the ability of these groups to coordinate with the metal centers, enhancing the stability and reactivity of the catalyst. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid (e.g., benzoic acid derivatives) generally lead to a high yield if they also contain additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups. This suggests that the aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while the additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with the metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers containing electron-withdrawing groups such as nitro (NO2) on an aromatic ring can lead to a high yield. This may be due to the increased acidity and coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups (e.g., octanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This might be due to their ability to enhance the hydrophobic environment around the catalyst, improving its activity.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

**End of Rules**

Rule Generator Message:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3H2]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and amino/hydroxy
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H][CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Polyols and carboxylic acid
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine and carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 9: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[nH][c][c][c][c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 10: Indole and amino acid
        ['[o][c][c][c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran and carboxylic acid
        ['[c][c](OC)[c](OC)[c]'],  # Rule 12: Dimethoxyphenyl group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H][CX4]'],  # Rule 13: Carboxylic acid and hydroxyl on aliphatic chain
        ['[n][c][CX4]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine and aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 9, 10, 11, 12, 14]:  # High yield rules
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Low yield rules
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Traditional Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current validation accuracy of 0.6571 is lower than the previous reference accuracies, which were consistently around 0.76. This suggests that the current rules may not be as effective in capturing the underlying patterns in the data.
   - The test accuracy is not provided for the current iteration, but the validation accuracy alone indicates a potential decline in model performance.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The consistent validation accuracy across previous iterations suggests that the model was stable. However, the drop in the current validation accuracy could indicate underfitting, where the model is not capturing the complexity of the data.
   - The SHAP values indicate that certain rules may not be generalizing well, leading to discrepancies between predicted and experimental values.

3. **Discrepancy Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, Rule 8 and Rule 9 often have high positive SHAP values. This suggests that these rules might be contributing to overestimation.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, Rule 6 often has a high negative SHAP value, indicating potential underestimation.

4. **Accuracy Improvement Interpretation:**
   - The decrease in validation accuracy suggests that the current rules may not be capturing the necessary features to improve model performance. This indicates a need for refinement and possibly the introduction of new rules or features.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis highlights specific rules that contribute significantly to prediction errors. For instance, Rule 8 and Rule 9 are frequently associated with overestimated loadings, while Rule 6 is linked to underestimated loadings.
   - These insights suggest that refining these rules could lead to improved model performance.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Rules with High Positive SHAP Values:**
   - **Rule 8 (Formyl Group on Aromatic Ring):** Consider revising this rule to account for additional functional groups that may influence coordination. The formyl group might not always interfere with coordination, especially if other groups enhance it.
   - **Rule 9 (Long Aliphatic Chains):** This rule could be too simplistic. Consider incorporating additional features such as chain branching or the presence of polar groups that might affect yield.

2. **Adjust Rules with High Negative SHAP Values:**
   - **Rule 6 (Fluorinated Alkyl Chains):** The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine might not always reduce coordination ability. Consider revising this rule to account for cases where fluorine's presence might enhance other interactions.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - Introduce new rules or features that capture interactions not currently considered. For example, consider the role of steric effects or electronic interactions that might not be fully captured by existing rules.
   - Use cross-validation techniques to ensure that the model is not overfitting to specific subsets of the data.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use the insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively test and refine rules. Focus on rules that consistently show high SHAP values for incorrect predictions.
   - Consider incorporating machine learning techniques to automatically suggest rule modifications based on SHAP value patterns.

By addressing these areas, the model's performance can be improved, leading to more accurate predictions of modifier loading on catalysts.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3H2]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and amino/hydroxy
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Polyols and carboxylic acid
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine and carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)(F)'],  # Rule 6: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 9: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[nH][c][c][c][c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 10: Indole and amino acid
        ['[o][c][c][c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran and carboxylic acid
        ['[c][c](OC)[c](OC)[c]'],  # Rule 12: Dimethoxyphenyl group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Carboxylic acid and hydroxyl on aliphatic chain
        ['[n][CX4]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine and aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 9, 10, 11, 12, 14]:  # High yield rules
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Low yield rules
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- ** Suggestion 9 **: For Rule 9, the SMARTS pattern `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']` should be checked to ensure it captures long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups. The current pattern may not account for all possible configurations of these chains. Consider using a more comprehensive pattern that includes variations in chain length.

- ** Suggestion 10 **: Rule 10's SMARTS pattern `['[nH][c][c][c][c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` should be reviewed to ensure it captures an indole ring and an amino acid moiety. The current pattern may not fully capture the indole nature. Consider refining the pattern to better match the rule description.

- ** Suggestion 11 **: For Rule 11, the SMARTS pattern `['[o][c][c][c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` should be checked to ensure it captures a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group. The current pattern may not account for all possible configurations of these groups. Consider using a more comprehensive pattern that includes variations in connectivity.

- ** Suggestion 12 **: Rule 12's SMARTS pattern `['[c][c](OC)[c](OC)[c]']` should be reviewed to ensure it captures a dimethoxyphenyl group. The current pattern may not fully capture the methoxy group positions. Consider refining the pattern to better match the rule description.

- ** Suggestion 13 **: For Rule 13, the SMARTS pattern `['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H]']` should be checked to ensure it captures a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain. The current pattern may not account for all possible configurations of these groups. Consider using a more comprehensive pattern that includes variations in connectivity.

- ** Suggestion 14 **: Rule 14's SMARTS pattern `['[n][CX4]']` should be reviewed to ensure it captures a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain. The current pattern may not fully capture the pyridine nature. Consider refining the pattern to better match the rule description.

- ** Suggestion 15 **: For Rule 15, the SMARTS pattern `['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]']` should be checked to ensure it captures a nitro group attached to an aromatic ring. The current pattern may not account for all possible configurations of these groups. Consider using a more comprehensive pattern that includes variations in connectivity.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3H2]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and amino/hydroxy
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Polyols and carboxylic acid
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine and carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)(F)'],  # Rule 6: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 9: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[nH][c][c][c][c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 10: Indole and amino acid
        ['[o][c][c][c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran and carboxylic acid
        ['[c][c](OC)[c](OC)[c]'],  # Rule 12: Dimethoxyphenyl group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Carboxylic acid and hydroxyl on aliphatic chain
        ['[n][CX4]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine and aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 9, 10, 11, 12, 14]:  # High yield rules
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Low yield rules
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
---------------------------------------------------------------
Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

- **Suggestion 12**: Rule 12's SMARTS `['[c][c](OC)[c](OC)[c]']` should be checked to ensure it captures dimethoxyphenyl groups correctly. Ensure that the methoxy groups are not part of a larger ether system that might not match the rule's intent.

- **Suggestion 13**: For Rule 13, the SMARTS `['[CX3](=O)[OX2H]', '[OX2H]']` should be checked to ensure it captures carboxylic acid and hydroxyl groups on aliphatic chains correctly. Consider specifying the presence of both groups on the same chain explicitly.

- **Suggestion 14**: Rule 14's SMARTS `['[n][CX4]']` should be checked to ensure it captures pyridine rings and aliphatic chains correctly. Ensure that the pyridine is not part of a larger heterocyclic system that might not match the rule's intent.

- **Suggestion 15**: For Rule 15, the SMARTS `['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]']` should be checked to ensure it captures nitro groups on aromatic rings correctly. Ensure that the nitro group is not part of a larger nitro-containing system that might not match the rule's intent.

### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules seem to have limited effectiveness, as indicated by the decrease in validation accuracy from previous iterations (0.76) to the current iteration (0.6286). This suggests that the rules may not be capturing the underlying patterns in the data effectively.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The decrease in validation accuracy suggests potential overfitting to the training data. The model may be too complex or the rules too specific, capturing noise rather than the true signal. The consistent high SHAP values for certain rules across different molecules, regardless of their experimental outcomes, further indicate overfitting.

3. **Discrepancy Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, Rule 6 and Rule 8 often have high positive SHAP values. This suggests these rules might be contributing to overestimations.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, Rule 6 and Rule 8 also show high negative SHAP values, indicating they might be contributing to underestimations.

4. **Accuracy Improvement Interpretation:**
   - The decrease in accuracy metrics suggests that the current rules are not improving the model's performance. The rules may need refinement to better capture the relationship between molecular features and catalyst loading.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis indicates that Rule 6 and Rule 8 are consistently influential in determining high loading predictions. This suggests these rules may need refinement to better align with experimental outcomes.
   - Rule 13, which often has negative SHAP values, might be contributing to underestimations and could be adjusted to improve predictions.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Rules with High Positive SHAP Values:**
   - **Rule 6 (Fluorinated Alkyl Chains):** Consider revising this rule to account for the context in which fluorinated chains might not reduce yield. Explore additional features or interactions that could modify its impact.
   - **Rule 8 (Formyl Group on Aromatic Ring):** Re-evaluate the conditions under which formyl groups lead to low yield. Consider interactions with other functional groups that might mitigate this effect.

2. **Adjust Rules with High Negative SHAP Values:**
   - **Rule 13 (Carboxylic Acid and Hydroxyl Group):** Investigate scenarios where these groups might enhance rather than reduce yield. Consider the influence of chain length or additional functional groups.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - Simplify rules to avoid overfitting. Focus on broader patterns rather than specific cases.
   - Introduce regularization techniques or cross-validation strategies to ensure the model generalizes well to unseen data.

4. **Iterative Refinement Using SHAP Insights:**
   - Use SHAP analysis to identify rules that consistently contribute to incorrect predictions. Refine these rules iteratively, testing their impact on validation accuracy.
   - Consider incorporating additional molecular descriptors or features that capture interactions not currently addressed by the rules.

By addressing these areas, the rules can be refined to improve model performance, reduce overfitting, and better align predictions with experimental outcomes.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3H2]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and amino/hydroxy
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Polyols and carboxylic acid
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine and carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)(F)'],  # Rule 6: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 9: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[nH][c][c][c][c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 10: Indole and amino acid
        ['[o][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran and carboxylic acid
        ['[c][OC][OC][c]'],  # Rule 12: Dimethoxyphenyl group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Carboxylic acid and hydroxyl on aliphatic chain
        ['[n][CX4]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine and aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]']  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):

                    else:  # Low yield rules
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3H2]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and amino/hydroxy
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Polyols and carboxylic acid
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine and carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)(F)'],  # Rule 6: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 9: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[nH][c][c][c][c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 10: Indole and amino acid
        ['[o][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran and carboxylic acid
        ['[c][OC][OC][c]'],  # Rule 12: Dimethoxyphenyl group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Carboxylic acid and hydroxyl on aliphatic chain
        ['[n][CX4]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine and aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]']  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 9, 10, 11, 12, 14]:  # High yield rules
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Low yield rules
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3H2]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and amino/hydroxy
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Polyols and carboxylic acid
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine and carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)(F)'],  # Rule 6: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 9: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[nH][c][c][c][c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 10: Indole and amino acid
        ['[o][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran and carboxylic acid
        ['[c][OC][OC][c]'],  # Rule 12: Dimethoxyphenyl group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Carboxylic acid and hydroxyl on aliphatic chain
        ['[n][CX4]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine and aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]']  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 9, 10, 11, 12, 14]:  # High yield rules
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Low yield rules
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Traditional Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules have shown some effectiveness, as indicated by the validation accuracy of 0.6857, which is an improvement from previous iterations. However, there is still room for improvement, as the accuracy is not significantly higher than the baseline reference metrics.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The consistent validation accuracy across iterations suggests that the model is not overfitting. However, the relatively low accuracy indicates potential underfitting, suggesting that the rules may not be capturing all the necessary features to accurately predict the loading of modifiers on catalysts.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, Rule 8 and Rule 9 often have high positive SHAP values, indicating these rules might be contributing to overestimation.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, Rule 6 and Rule 9 have high negative SHAP values, suggesting these rules might be contributing to underestimation.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The slight improvement in accuracy suggests that the current rules are moving in the right direction, but further refinement is needed to achieve significant improvements.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis indicates that Rule 8 and Rule 9 are frequently associated with discrepancies in predictions. This suggests that these rules may need to be refined to better capture the nuances of the data.
   - Rule 6, which is associated with low yield predictions, might be too restrictive and could be adjusted to allow for more flexibility in predictions.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Rules with High Positive SHAP Values:**
   - **Rule 8:** Consider revising the conditions under which a formyl group leads to low yield. It may be beneficial to explore additional functional groups or structural contexts that could mitigate the negative impact of the formyl group.
   - **Rule 9:** Re-evaluate the impact of long aliphatic chains. Consider incorporating additional features or interactions that could influence the yield, such as branching or the presence of other functional groups.

2. **Adjust Rules with High Negative SHAP Values:**
   - **Rule 6:** Reassess the impact of fluorinated alkyl chains. It may be useful to explore scenarios where these chains do not significantly hinder coordination, potentially by considering the overall molecular context or the presence of other coordinating groups.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - Introduce additional rules or modify existing ones to capture more complex interactions and features that may be influencing the loading of modifiers on catalysts. This could involve incorporating machine learning techniques to identify patterns not currently captured by the rules.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively test and refine rules. This could involve creating new rules based on observed patterns in the data or adjusting existing rules to better align with experimental outcomes.

5. **Incorporate Additional Data:**
   - If possible, gather more data to enhance the training set, which could help improve the model's ability to generalize and reduce underfitting.

By addressing these areas, the rules can be refined to improve the accuracy and reliability of predictions, ultimately leading to better performance in predicting the loading of modifiers on catalysts.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3H2]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and amino/hydroxy
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Polyols and carboxylic acid
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine and carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)(F)'],  # Rule 6: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 9: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[nH]1c2ccccc2c3c1cccc3', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 10: Indole and amino acid
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran and carboxylic acid
        ['[c]1cc(OC)c(OC)cc1'],  # Rule 12: Dimethoxyphenyl group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Carboxylic acid and hydroxyl on aliphatic chain
        ['[n][CX4]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine and aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 9, 10, 11, 12, 14]:  # High yield rules
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Low yield rules
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran and carboxylic acid
        ['[c]1cc(OC)c(OC)cc1'],  # Rule 12: Dimethoxyphenyl group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Carboxylic acid and hydroxyl on aliphatic chain
        ['[n][CX4]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine and aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 9, 10, 11, 12, 14]:  # High yield rules
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Low yield rules
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3H2]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and amino/hydroxy
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H][OX2H][OX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Polyols and carboxylic acid
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine and carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)(F)'],  # Rule 6: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 9: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[nH][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 10: Indole and amino acid
        ['[o][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran and carboxylic acid
        ['[c][OX2][c][OX2]'],  # Rule 12: Dimethoxyphenyl
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H][CX4]'],  # Rule 13: Carboxylic acid and hydroxyl on aliphatic chain
        ['[n][CX4]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine and aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[OX-]'],  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 9, 10, 11, 12, 14]:  # High yield rules
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Low yield rules
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- **Focus on High Lift and Confidence**: Prioritize rules that have shown higher lift and confidence in previous iterations. Analyzing these rules might provide insights into which conditions are most effective and could be further optimized.

- **Iterative Testing and Validation**: Continue iterating on the rules and validate them against new data to ensure they maintain or improve their performance. This iterative process can help in fine-tuning the rules to achieve better metrics.

Overall, while the current rules are performing reasonably well, there is potential for improvement, particularly in increasing confidence and lift to enhance the predictive power and applicability of the rules.
