### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules seem to have a moderate level of effectiveness, as indicated by the validation accuracy of 0.6571. This is slightly lower than some of the previous accuracies (e.g., 0.6857), suggesting that the rules may not be fully optimized yet.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The consistent validation accuracy across different iterations suggests that the model is not overfitting. However, the lower accuracy compared to some previous iterations indicates potential underfitting, where the model might not be capturing all the necessary patterns in the data.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 6, Rule 8, Rule 9) might be contributing to overestimation. These rules should be scrutinized for potential refinement.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 6, Rule 8) might be causing underestimation and need adjustment.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The current accuracy metrics suggest that there is room for improvement. The validation accuracy has not significantly improved over iterations, indicating that the current rules might be reaching a local minimum. Further refinement is necessary to enhance the model's performance.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis highlights specific rules that consistently contribute to high or low predictions. For instance, Rule 6 and Rule 8 often have significant SHAP values, indicating their strong influence on predictions. This suggests that these rules might need refinement to better align with experimental outcomes.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Overestimated Rules:**
   - Rules with high positive SHAP values for overestimated loadings, such as Rule 6 (fluorinated alkyl chains) and Rule 8 (formyl group on aromatic rings), should be revisited. Consider incorporating additional conditions or modifying the existing criteria to better capture the nuances of these modifiers.

2. **Adjust Underestimated Rules:**
   - Rules with high negative SHAP values for underestimated loadings, such as Rule 6 and Rule 8, should be adjusted. This could involve relaxing some constraints or adding new features that might enhance the rule's predictive power.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - To address potential underfitting, consider expanding the feature set or introducing new rules that capture additional chemical properties or interactions. This could help the model generalize better across different datasets.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. Focus on rules that consistently show high SHAP values and explore ways to improve their alignment with experimental data. This iterative process can help in gradually enhancing the model's accuracy and reliability.

5. **Evaluate Rule Effectiveness:**
   - Continuously evaluate the effectiveness of refined rules by monitoring changes in validation accuracy and SHAP values. This will help in identifying which modifications lead to tangible improvements and guide further iterations.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

Rule Generator Message:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:

        ['[OX2H,OX1-;$([OX2H,OX1-][CX4;!$(C([OX2H,OX1-])[O,S,#7,#15])])]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],
        ['[OX2;$([OX2][C;!$([C]([OX2])[O,S,#7,#15,F,Cl,Br,I])])][C;!$([C]([OX2])[O,S,#7,#15])]', '[OX2;$([OX2][c])][c]'],
        ['[CX3H]=[OX1][c]'],
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],
        ['[nH][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],
        ['[o][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2][c]'],
        ['[OX2H,OX1-;$([OX2H,OX1-][CX4;!$(C([OX2H,OX1-])[O,S,#7,#15])])][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],
        ['[n][CX4]'],
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[OX1-]']
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 9, 10, 11, 12, 14]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
---------------------------------------------------------------
Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;$([N][c])]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl group with carboxylic acid and amino/hydroxy
        ['[SX2H;$([SX2H][CX4;!$(C([SX2H])~[O,S,#7,#15])])]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H,OX1-;$([OX2H,OX1-][CX4;!$(C([OX2H,OX1-])[O,S,#7,#15])])]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Polyols and carboxylic acid
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine and carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[OX2;$([OX2][C;!$([C]([OX2])[O,S,#7,#15,F,Cl,Br,I])])][C;!$([C]([OX2])[O,S,#7,#15])]', '[OX2;$([OX2][c])][c]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy groups
        ['[CX3H]=[OX1][c]'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 9: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[nH][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 10: Indole ring and amino acid
        ['[o][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran and carboxylic acid
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2][c]'],  # Rule 12: Dimethoxyphenyl group
        ['[OX2H,OX1-;$([OX2H,OX1-][CX4;!$(C([OX2H,OX1-])[O,S,#7,#15])])][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 13: Hydroxyl and carboxylic acid on aliphatic chain
        ['[n][CX4]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine and aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[OX1-]']  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 9, 10, 11, 12, 14]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;!$([N][!C])]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group

        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[OX2;$([OX2][C;!$([C]([OX2])[O,S,#7,#15,F,Cl,Br,I])])][C;!$([C]([OX2])[O,S,#7,#15])]', '[OX2;$([OX2][c])][c]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy groups

        ['[nH][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 10: Indole ring and amino acid
        ['[o][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran and carboxylic acid
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][OX2][c]'],  # Rule 12: Dimethoxyphenyl group

    ]

        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))

                        row.append(1)

                else:

            except:

        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Traditional Commenter Message:
### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules seem to have limited effectiveness, as indicated by the validation accuracy of 0.6286, which is lower than the previous reference accuracies (0.76). This suggests that the rules may not be capturing the underlying patterns effectively.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The consistent validation accuracy across iterations suggests potential underfitting. The model may not be complex enough to capture the nuances in the data, or the rules may not be sufficiently detailed to differentiate between high and low loading accurately.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, Rule 6 and Rule 9 often have high positive SHAP values. This indicates that these rules might be contributing to overestimations.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, Rule 6 and Rule 9 also show significant negative SHAP values, suggesting they might be causing underestimations.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The current accuracy metrics do not suggest significant improvement over previous iterations. The model's performance has not reached a local minimum, indicating that further refinement of the rules is necessary.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis highlights that Rule 6 (fluorinated alkyl chains) and Rule 9 (long aliphatic chains) are frequently associated with discrepancies in predictions. This suggests that these rules may need refinement to better capture the impact of these structural features on loading.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Rules with High Positive SHAP Values:**
   - **Rule 6:** Consider revising the impact of fluorinated alkyl chains. While they are generally associated with low yield, the current rule may not account for exceptions where other functional groups mitigate the electron-withdrawing effects of fluorine.
   - **Rule 9:** Re-evaluate the influence of long aliphatic chains. Introduce additional conditions or sub-rules to account for cases where other functional groups enhance coordination despite the presence of long chains.

2. **Adjust Rules with High Negative SHAP Values:**
   - **Rule 6 and Rule 9:** These rules should be adjusted to better capture the conditions under which they lead to low loading predictions. Consider incorporating interactions with other functional groups that may alter their expected impact.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - Introduce more nuanced rules that consider the interplay between different functional groups. This could help address underfitting by capturing more complex patterns in the data.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. For example, if a rule consistently shows high SHAP values for incorrect predictions, investigate the structural features of those molecules to identify potential modifications to the rule.

5. **Incorporate Additional Features:**
   - Consider adding new features or rules that capture other relevant chemical properties, such as steric effects or electronic properties, which may influence the loading of modifiers on catalysts.

By implementing these recommendations, the rules can be refined to improve the model's accuracy and generalization, ultimately leading to better predictions of modifier loading on catalysts.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3H2]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and amino/hydroxy
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Polyols and carboxylic acid
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine and carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)(F)'],  # Rule 6: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 9: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[nH]1[cH][cH][cH][cH][cH]1', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 10: Indole and amino acid
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran and carboxylic acid
        ['[c]1cc(OC)c(OC)cc1'],  # Rule 12: Dimethoxyphenyl group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Carboxylic acid and hydroxyl on aliphatic chain
        ['[n][CX4]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine and aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 10, 11, 12, 14]:  # High yield rules
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Low yield rules
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
---------------------------------------------------------------
Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3H2]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and amino/hydroxy
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Polyols and carboxylic acid
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine and carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)(F)'],  # Rule 6: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 9: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[nH]1[cH][cH][cH][cH][cH]1', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 10: Indole and amino acid
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran and carboxylic acid
        ['[c]1cc(OC)c(OC)cc1'],  # Rule 12: Dimethoxyphenyl group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Carboxylic acid and hydroxyl on aliphatic chain
        ['[n][CX4]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine and aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 10, 11, 12, 14]:  # High yield rules
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Low yield rules
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

   - The consistent performance across different datasets suggests that the model is not overfitting to the training data, but the moderate accuracy indicates potential underfitting.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 6, Rule 8, Rule 9) may be contributing to overestimation.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 6, Rule 8) may be contributing to underestimation.

### Recommendations for Improvement

2. **Adjust Rules with High Negative SHAP Values:**

3. **Improve Generalization:**

5. **Evaluate Rule Effectiveness:**

By following these recommendations, the current rules can be refined to improve the model's accuracy and generalization, ultimately leading to better predictions of catalyst loading.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3H2]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and amino/hydroxy
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Polyols and carboxylic acid
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine and carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)(F)'],  # Rule 6: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 9: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[nH][c][c][c][c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 10: Indole and amino acid
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran and carboxylic acid
        ['[c]1cc(OC)c(OC)cc1'],  # Rule 12: Dimethoxyphenyl group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1][CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Carboxylic acid and hydroxyl on aliphatic chain
        ['[n][CX4]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine and aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 9, 10, 11, 12, 14]:  # High yield rules
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Low yield rules
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3H2]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and amino/hydroxy
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Polyols and carboxylic acid
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine and carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)(F)'],  # Rule 6: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 9: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[nH][c][c][c][c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 10: Indole and amino acid
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran and carboxylic acid
        ['[c]1cc(OC)c(OC)cc1'],  # Rule 12: Dimethoxyphenyl group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1][CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Carboxylic acid and hydroxyl on aliphatic chain
        ['[n][CX4]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine and aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 9, 10, 11, 12, 14]:  # High yield rules
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Low yield rules
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

- ** Suggestion 1 **: For Rule 1, the SMARTS pattern `['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2]']` is correct for identifying carboxylic acid and amino groups. However, ensure that the amino group is not part of an aromatic system, as the rule specifies aliphatic amino groups.

- ** Suggestion 2 **: For Rule 2, the SMARTS pattern `['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3H2]', '[c][OX2H]']` should be refined to ensure that the phenyl group is directly attached to the carboxylic acid and that additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy are present. Consider using a pattern that ensures the phenyl group is directly connected to the carboxylic acid.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: For Rule 3, the SMARTS pattern `['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` is appropriate for identifying sulfanyl and carboxylic acid groups. Ensure that the sulfanyl group is not part of a larger sulfur-containing functional group that might not match the rule's intent.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: For Rule 4, the SMARTS pattern `['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H]']` should be adjusted to specifically identify polyols with multiple hydroxyl groups. Consider using a pattern that captures multiple hydroxyl groups in proximity to the carboxylic acid.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: For Rule 5, the SMARTS pattern `['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` is correct for identifying pyridine and carboxylic acid groups. Ensure that the pyridine is not part of a larger heterocyclic system that might not match the rule's intent.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: For Rule 6, the SMARTS pattern `['[CX4](F)(F)(F)']` should be expanded to capture longer fluorinated alkyl chains, as the rule specifies chains, not just trifluoromethyl groups.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: For Rule 7, the SMARTS pattern `['[OX2][CX4][OX2]']` should be refined to ensure it captures methoxy groups specifically attached to aliphatic chains or aromatic rings, as the rule specifies.

- ** Suggestion 8 **: For Rule 8, the SMARTS pattern `['[c][CX3H]=O']` is correct for identifying formyl groups on aromatic rings. Ensure that the formyl group is directly attached to the aromatic system.

- ** Suggestion 9 **: For Rule 9, the SMARTS pattern `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']` should be adjusted to capture long aliphatic chains more effectively. Consider using a pattern that captures chains of a specific length or longer.

- ** Suggestion 10 **: For Rule 10, the SMARTS pattern `['[nH][c][c][c][c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` should be refined to ensure it captures indole rings with an amino acid moiety, as the rule specifies.

- ** Suggestion 11 **: For Rule 11, the SMARTS pattern `['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']` is correct for identifying benzofuran and carboxylic acid groups. Ensure that the benzofuran is not part of a larger fused ring system that might not match the rule's intent.

- ** Suggestion 12 **: For Rule 12, the SMARTS pattern `['[c]1cc(OC)c(OC)cc1']` should be refined to ensure it captures dimethoxyphenyl groups specifically, as the rule specifies.

- ** Suggestion 13 **: For Rule 13, the SMARTS pattern `['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1][CX4][OX2H]']` should be adjusted to ensure it captures carboxylic acid and hydroxyl groups on aliphatic chains, as the rule specifies.

- ** Suggestion 14 **: For Rule 14, the SMARTS pattern `['[n][CX4]']` should be refined to ensure it captures pyridine rings with aliphatic chains, as the rule specifies.

- ** Suggestion 15 **: For Rule 15, the SMARTS pattern `['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]']` is correct for identifying nitro groups on aromatic rings. Ensure that the nitro group is directly attached to the aromatic system.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[NX3H2]'],  # Rule 1: Carboxylic acid and amino group
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3H2]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 2: Phenyl with carboxylic acid and amino/hydroxy
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 3: Sulfanyl and carboxylic acid
        ['[OX2H][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Polyols and carboxylic acid
        ['[n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine and carboxylic acid
        ['[CX4](F)(F)(F)'],  # Rule 6: Fluorinated alkyl chains
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy groups
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 9: Long aliphatic chains
        ['[nH][c][c][c][c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 10: Indole and amino acid
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran and carboxylic acid
        ['[c]1cc(OC)c(OC)cc1'],  # Rule 12: Dimethoxyphenyl group
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1][CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 13: Carboxylic acid and hydroxyl on aliphatic chain
        ['[n][CX4]'],  # Rule 14: Pyridine and aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[O-]'],  # Rule 15: Nitro group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 9, 10, 11, 12, 14]:  # High yield rules
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Low yield rules
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current validation accuracy of 0.6857 is slightly lower than the previous reference accuracies, which were consistently around 0.76. This suggests that the current rules may not be as effective as the previous iterations in capturing the underlying patterns in the data.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The consistent validation accuracy across different iterations suggests that the model is not overfitting. However, the lower accuracy compared to previous iterations indicates potential underfitting, where the model may not be capturing all relevant features or interactions.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 6, Rule 8, Rule 9) may be contributing to overestimation. These rules should be scrutinized for potential refinement.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 6, Rule 8) may be causing underestimation and should be adjusted.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The current accuracy metrics suggest that there is room for improvement. The iterative process has not yet reached a local minimum, indicating that further refinement of the rules could enhance performance.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis highlights specific rules that consistently contribute to incorrect predictions. For instance, Rule 6 and Rule 8 often have significant SHAP values, indicating their strong influence on predictions. These rules may need to be refined to better align with experimental outcomes.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Overestimated Loading Rules:**
   - Rules with high positive SHAP values for overestimated loadings, such as Rule 6 (fluorinated alkyl chains) and Rule 8 (formyl group on aromatic rings), should be revisited. Consider incorporating additional conditions or exceptions to these rules to reduce their influence on predictions.

2. **Adjust Underestimated Loading Rules:**
   - Rules with high negative SHAP values for underestimated loadings, such as Rule 6 and Rule 8, should be adjusted. This could involve relaxing some constraints or adding new features that capture missing interactions.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - To address potential underfitting, consider expanding the feature set or incorporating additional data sources. This could involve exploring new chemical descriptors or interactions that are not currently captured by the existing rules.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. This could involve testing new hypotheses about chemical interactions or revising existing rules based on observed discrepancies between predictions and experimental values.

5. **Evaluate Rule Effectiveness:**
   - Continuously evaluate the effectiveness of refined rules through cross-validation and SHAP analysis. This iterative process will help identify which rules contribute positively to model performance and which require further adjustment.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing both a carboxylic acid group (COOH) and an amino group (NH2) tend to result in a high yield. These groups can coordinate with metal centers, enhancing catalyst stability and reactivity. Examples include (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid and 5-aminopentanoic acid.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a phenyl group attached to a carboxylic acid and additional functional groups like amino or hydroxy groups generally lead to a high yield. The aromatic ring may facilitate π-π interactions, while additional groups enhance coordination. Examples include 4-aminobenzoic acid and 5-(4-hydroxyphenyl)pentanoic acid.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing a sulfanyl group (SH) and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The thiol group can form strong interactions with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst. An example is 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with multiple hydroxyl groups (polyols) and a carboxylic acid group generally lead to a high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can enhance solubility and coordination with metal centers. An example is (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers. An example is pyridine-3-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with fluorinated alkyl chains tend to result in a low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of fluorine may reduce the coordination ability of the carboxylic acid group. An example is 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with methoxy groups (OCH3) attached to an aliphatic chain or an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. This could be due to steric hindrance or reduced coordination ability. An example is 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (CHO) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a low yield. The formyl group may interfere with the coordination of the carboxylic acid group. Examples include 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid and 4-formylbenzoic acid.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with long aliphatic chains without additional functional groups tend to result in a low yield. The lack of polar or coordinating groups may reduce interaction with the catalyst. An example is octanoic acid.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an indole ring and an amino acid moiety tend to result in a high yield. The indole ring can provide π-π interactions, and the amino acid moiety can enhance coordination. An example is (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran ring and a carboxylic acid group tend to result in a high yield. The benzofuran ring can facilitate π-π interactions, enhancing the catalyst's reactivity. An example is 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a dimethoxyphenyl group tend to result in a high yield. The methoxy groups on the phenyl ring can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a hydroxyl group on an aliphatic chain tend to result in a low yield. The presence of these groups may not provide sufficient coordination or interaction with the catalyst. An example is 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and an aliphatic chain tend to result in a high yield. The pyridine ring can enhance coordination with metal centers, and the aliphatic chain can provide flexibility. An example is 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a nitro group (NO2) attached to an aromatic ring tend to result in a high yield. The nitro group can enhance electron density and coordination ability. An example is 4-nitrobenzoic acid.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------
